Michael Worboys, [3mSpreading Germs: Disease Theories and Medical Practice in Britain, 1865โ1900 [0m(Cambridge: Cambridge University 
Press, 2000). A subtle investigation of the impact of bacteriology and germs theories on British medicine.

Michael Bliss, [3mThe Discovery of Insulin [0m(Edinburgh: Harris, 1983). A balanced account of this famous episode in the history of 
medicine. 

Thomas Neville Bonner, [3mBecoming a Physician: Medical Education in Great Britain, France, Germany and the United States, 1750โ1945 [0m
(Oxford and New York: Oxford University Press, 1995). A fine comparative study, with many resonances for earlier chapters of this 
Introduction as well. 

Roger Cooter and John Pickstone (eds), [3mMedicine in the Twentieth Century [0m(Amsterdam: Harwood Academic Publishers, 2000). A large 
collection of essays on many aspects of medicine in the last century. 

John Farley, [3mThe International Health Division of the Rockefeller Foundation: The Russell Years, 1920โ1934 [0m(Cambridge: Cambridge 
University Press, 1995). An excellent introduction to the important dimension of international health, and the Americanization of 
the world. 

Joel Howell, [3mTechnology in the Hospital: Transforming Patient Care in the Early Twentieth Century [0m(Baltimore: Johns Hopkins 
University Press, 1995). A fine monograph on how medical science and technology influenced what doctors did in the hospital. 

James Le Fanu, [3mThe Rise and Fall of Modern Medicine [0m(London: Little, Brown and Co., 1999). A perceptive account of 20th-century 
medicine by a shrewd general practitioner and medical journalist. 

Harry Marks, [3mThe Progress of Experiment: Science and Therapeutic Reform in the United States, 1900โ1990 [0m(Cambridge: Cambridge 
University Press, 1997). An excellent introduction to the clinical trial, and much else besides. 

Rosemary Stevens, [3mIn Sickness and in Wealth: American Hospitals in the Twentieth Century [0m(New York: Basic Books, 1989). A full 
analysis of the economic and medical dimensions of American hospitals.
